id="i5cbb536cb37a41f98148878049be697f_4"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:63pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:18pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Q4 Results and Forecast</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Revenue in Q4 grew 12% year over year, or 13% on a foreign exchange (F&#47;X) neutral basis.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:7.15pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-3.85pt;vertical-align:baseline">1</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> Our healthy top line growth reflects the benefits of paid sharing, our recent price changes and the strength of our underlying business driven by a strong slate. Revenue was $0.1B (2%) above our October forecast due to favorable F&#47;X movement and stronger than anticipated membership growth. Paid net additions totaled 13.1M in Q4&#8217;23 vs. 7.7M in Q4&#8217;22 &#8212; our largest Q4 ever. ARM</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:7.15pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-3.85pt;vertical-align:baseline">2</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> was up 1% year over year on both a reported and F&#47;X neutral basis. This was in-line with our expectations of &#8220;roughly flat year-over-year&#8221; ARM due to limited price increases over the last 18 months, as well as price reductions in some countries early in 2023, which were partially offset by price rises in the US, UK and France in Q4&#8217;23. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">In Q4&#8217;23, operating income amounted to $1.5B, up from $0.5B in the year ago period, while operating margin improved to 17% vs. 7% in the year ago quarter. We under-forecasted both operating income and operating margin (forecast of $1.2B and 13%, respectively) due to the revenue upside in the quarter and lower-than-planned spending. For 2023, we generated $7B of operating income, up 23% year over year. Operating margin for 2023 was 21% (both reported and using F&#47;X rates at the beginning of 2023) &#8212;  ahead of our 18%-20% beginning-of-year forecast.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">EPS for the fourth quarter was $2.11 compared with $0.12 last year and our forecast of $2.15. EPS includes a $239 million non-cash unrealized loss from F&#47;X remeasurement on our Euro denominated debt (due to the intra-quarter depreciation of the US dollar against most currencies). </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">As a reminder, the quarterly guidance we provide is our actual internal forecast at the time we report. Our primary financial metrics are revenue for growth and operating margin for profitability. Our goals are to sustain healthy revenue growth, expand operating margin and deliver growing free cash flow.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">We enter 2024 with good momentum. We expect healthy double digit revenue growth for the full year 2024 on a F&#47;X neutral basis driven by continued membership growth as well as improvement in F&#47;X neutral ARM as we adjust prices. We&#8217;ll also continue to invest in and build our ads business&#59; we expect strong growth in 2024 but off a small base so it&#8217;s not yet a primary driver of our overall revenue growth. Our aim is to make ads a more substantial revenue stream that contributes to sustained, healthy revenue growth in 2025 and beyond.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Our forecast for Q1&#8217;24 revenue growth of 13% includes a three percentage point headwind from F&#47;X on a year over year basis, primarily due to the large decrease in the </font><font style="color:#3051f2;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;text-decoration:underline">Argentine peso</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:7.15pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-3.85pt;vertical-align:baseline">3</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> relative to the US dollar. Therefore, we expect revenue to increase 16% on a F&#47;X neutral basis in Q1&#8217;24. Similar to prior years, we expect paid net additions to be down sequentially (reflecting typical seasonality as well as some likely pull forward from our strong Q4&#8217;23 performance) but to be up versus Q1&#8217;23 paid net adds of 1.8M. We expect global ARM to be up year over year on a F&#47;X neutral basis in Q1.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">We are increasing our full year 2024 operating margin forecast from 22%-23% to 24% (based on F&#47;X rates as of January 1, 2024). This reflects the weakening of the US dollar vs. most other currencies since October as well as our stronger-than-forecasted Q4&#8217;23 performance and our expectation for how that will carry through 2024. As we noted in our Q3 letter, while we've launched a F&#47;X risk management</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:2pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:8pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">__________________________________</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:5.2pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-2.8pt;vertical-align:baseline">1</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:8pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> Excluding the year over year effect of foreign exchange rate movements. Assumes foreign exchange rates remained constant with foreign exchange rates from each of the corresponding months of the prior-year period. </font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:5.2pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-2.8pt;vertical-align:baseline">2 </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:8pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">ARM (Average Revenue per Membership) is defined as streaming revenue divided by the average number of streaming paid memberships divided by the number of months in the period. These figures do not include sales taxes or VAT.</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:5.2pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-2.8pt;vertical-align:baseline">3 </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:8pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">https&#58;&#47;&#47;www.google.com&#47;finance&#47;quote&#47;ARS-USD&#63;sa&#61;X&#38;ved&#61;2ahUKEwiJzZjyw-iDAxWpM0QIHRqlCooQmY0JegQIHhAv&#38;window&#61;1Y</font></div><div style="height:63pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div><table style="border-collapse:collapse;display:inline-table;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:100.000%"><tr><td style="width:1.0%"></td><td style="width:25.182%"></td><td style="width:0.1%"></td><td style="width:1.0%"></td><td style="width:72.618%"></td><td style="width:0.1%"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="padding:0 1pt"><div><img alt="nflxlogo2015a22a.jpg" src="nflxlogo2015a22a.jpg" style="height:22px;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:86px"></div></td><td colspan="3" style="padding:2px 1pt;text-align:left;vertical-align:top"><div style="text-align:right"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:100%">2</font></div></td></tr></table></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:63pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">program with a goal of reducing near term volatility, we aren't fully hedged, which is why we are still guiding and managing to a F&#47;X neutral operating margin target. Our goal is to steadily increase our operating margin each year, though the rate of margin expansion may vary year to year. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:18pt;font-weight:700;line-height:111%">2024 Perspective</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Entertainment has always been a fast changing industry &#8212; with new technology and consumer behavior patterns creating new business models. Choice and control are the price of entry in modern entertainment, and that is streaming. It&#8217;s what consumers want, and we believe it&#8217;s the best way for our industry to stay relevant and growing. As Netflix has shown, it can also be a very healthy business.  Since our global launch in 2016, we&#8217;ve been able to invest heavily in our slate &#8212; with content amortization up almost 3X from $4.8B in 2016 to $14.2B in 2023 &#8212; while steadily increasing our operating margins (up more than 5X, from 4% to 21% over the same period) and growing our free cash flow (from negative $3.3B in 2019 to positive $6.9B in 2023).</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">As our competitors adjust to these changes, it&#8217;s logical to expect further consolidation, particularly among companies with large and declining linear networks. We&#8217;re not interested in acquiring linear assets. Nor do we believe that further M&#38;A among traditional entertainment companies will materially change the competitive environment given all the consolidation that has already happened over the last decade (Viacom&#47;CBS, AT&#38;T&#47;Time Warner, Disney&#47;Fox, Time Warner&#47;Discovery, etc.). But we expect our industry to remain highly competitive given&#58; the franchise strength and programming expertise within traditional entertainment companies&#59; ongoing heavy investment from large tech players like YouTube, Amazon and Apple&#59; and broader competition for people&#8217;s time, including gaming and social media (TikTok, Instagram etc.). It&#8217;s why continuing to improve our entertainment offering is so important, and as many of our competitors cut back on their content spend, we continue to invest in our slate. In FY24, we expect a high single digit percentage year over year increase in content amortization.  </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">If we continue to execute well and drive continuous improvement &#8212; with a better slate, easier discovery and more fandom &#8212; while establishing ourselves in new areas like advertising and games, we believe we have a lot more room to grow. It&#8217;s a $600B+ opportunity revenue market across pay TV, film, games and branded advertising &#8212; and today Netflix accounts for only roughly 5% of that addressable market. And our share of TV viewing is still less than 10% in every country. But it all starts with the consumer. Because when we delight our members, we can drive more engagement, revenue and profit than the competition &#8212; creating an increasingly valuable entertainment company (for our members, content creators and shareholders) that will strengthen and grow over time.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="height:63pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div Because when people regularly press play and stay, they&#8217;re happier and place a higher value on our service &#8212; which means they stick around longer (retention) and recommend Netflix to their friends (acquisition).</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:18pt;font-weight:700;line-height:115%">Monetization</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Over the last few years we&#8217;ve increased sophistication on our pricing and plans strategy so that we can more effectively capture the value created by our service. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">First</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">, pricing. We seek to provide a range of prices and plans to meet a wide range of needs, including highly competitive starting prices. As we invest in and improve Netflix, we&#8217;ll occasionally ask our members to pay a little extra to reflect those improvements, which in turn helps drive the positive flywheel of additional investment to further improve and grow our service.  </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Second</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">, ads. Scaling our ads business represents an opportunity to tap into significant new revenue and profit pools over the medium to longer term. In Q4&#8216;23, like the quarter before, our ads membership increased by nearly 70% quarter over quarter, supported by improvements in our offering (e.g., downloads) and the phasing out of our Basic plan for new and rejoining members in our ads markets. The ads plan now accounts for 40% of all Netflix sign-ups in our ads markets and we&#8217;re looking to retire our Basic plan in some of our ads countries, starting with Canada and the UK in Q2 and taking it from there. On the advertiser side, we continue to improve the targeting and measurement we offer our customers. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Third</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">, monetizing sharing. We believe we've successfully addressed account sharing, ensuring that when people enjoy Netflix they pay for the service too. Features like Transfer Profile and Extra Member were much requested, and many millions of our members are now taking advantage of them. At this stage, paid sharing is our normal course of business &#8212; creating a much bigger base from which we can grow and enabling us to more effectively penetrate the near term addressable market of &#126;500M connected TV households (excluding China and Russia), which should increase over time as broadband penetration rises.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="height:63pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div><table style="border-collapse:collapse;display:inline-table;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:100.000%"><tr><td style="width:1.0%"></td><td style="width:25.182%"></td><td style="width:0.1%"></td><td style="width:1.0%"></td><td style="width:72.618%"></td><td style="width:0.1%"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="padding:0 1pt"><div><img alt="nflxlogo2015a22a.jpg" src="nflxlogo2015a22a.jpg" style="height:22px;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:86px"></div></td><td colspan="3" style="padding:2px 1pt;text-align:left;vertical-align:top"><div style="text-align:right"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:100%">6</font></div></td></tr></table></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:63pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:18pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Cash Flow and Capital Structure</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Net cash provided by operating activities in Q4 was $1.7B vs. $0.4B in the prior year period. Free cash flow (FCF)</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:7.15pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-3.85pt;vertical-align:baseline">14</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> for Q4 was $1.6B vs. $0.3B in the prior year period. For the full year 2023, net cash provided by operating activities was $7.3B vs. $2.0B in 2022 while FCF totaled $6.9B compared to $1.6B in 2022. This included approximately $1B in delayed spending due to the WGA and SAG-AFTRA strikes. Over the past four years, we&#8217;ve generated $12B in net cash provided by operating activities and over $10B in positive FCF, recouping the $9B in net cash used in operating activities and $10B FCF deficit we generated from 2016-2019, when we invested heavily to build our original programming and production capabilities around the world.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><img alt="cumulativefcfa.jpg" src="cumulativefcfa.jpg" style="height:292px;margin-bottom:5pt;vertical-align:text-bottom;width:575px"></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">As we&#8217;ve said previously, the strikes will cause some lumpiness in our year to year FCF progression. For the full year 2024, assuming no material swings in F&#47;X, we currently expect FCF of approximately $6B. We continue to expect 2024 cash spend on content of up to $17B. In Q4&#8217;23, we repurchased 5.5M shares for $2.5B and we have $8.4B remaining under our current buyback authorization. We have $400M in senior notes maturing in Q1 of this year and we plan to pay that down with cash on hand.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:18pt;font-weight:700;line-height:115%">Environmental, Social, and Governance (ESG)</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">We continue to evolve our executive compensation model to address feedback from shareholders. As outlined in our </font><font style="color:#3051f2;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;text-decoration:underline">8-K</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:7.15pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%;position:relative;top:-3.85pt;vertical-align:baseline">15</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%"> filed on December 8, 2023, the 2024 program reflects several key changes including&#58; expanding participation in the performance-based bonus program to include our CFO, Chief Legal Officer and Executive Chairman (in addition to our co-CEOs), eliminating the ability to allocate compensation between cash and stock options, and granting long-term equity compensation in the form of RSUs and PSUs (tied to total shareholder return relative to the S&#38;P 500) in lieu of stock options.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:2pt"><font equipment and change in other assets.</font></div><div><font id="i5cbb536cb37a41f98148878049be697f_7"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-top:8pt"><font style="color:#666666;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Use of Non-GAAP Measures</font></div><div><font style="color:#222222;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">This shareholder letter and its attachments include reference to the non-GAAP financial measures of F&#47;X neutral revenue and adjusted operating profit and margin, and free cash flow. Management believes that free cash flow is an important liquidity metric because it measures, during a given period, the amount of cash generated that is available to repay debt obligations, make strategic acquisitions and investments and for certain other activities like stock repurchases. Management believes that F&#47;X neutral revenue and adjusted operating profit and margin allow investors to compare our projected results to our actual results absent intra-year currency fluctuations and the impact of restructuring costs. However, these non-GAAP financial measures should be considered in addition to, not as a substitute for or superior to, net income, operating income (profit), operating margin, diluted earnings per share and net cash provided by (used in) operating activities, or other financial measures prepared in accordance with GAAP. Reconciliation to the GAAP equivalent of these non-GAAP measures are contained in tabular form on the attached unaudited financial statements and in the F&#47;X neutral operating margin disclosure above. We are not able to reconcile forward-looking non-GAAP financial measures because we are unable to predict without unreasonable effort the exact amount or timing of the reconciling items, including property and equipment and change in other assets, and the impact of changes in currency exchange rates. The variability of these items could have a significant impact on our future GAAP financial results.</font></div><div style="margin-top:8pt"><font style="color:#666666;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%">Forward-Looking Statements</font></div><div><font style="color:#222222;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">This shareholder letter contains certain forward-looking statements within the meaning of the federal securities laws, including statements regarding our expected results for the fiscal quarter ending March 31, 2024 and fiscal year ending December 31, 2024&#59; adoption and growth of streaming entertainment&#59; growth outlook and market opportunity&#59; competitive landscape and position&#59; core strategy and business model&#59; content offerings, including content licensing&#59; slate strength&#59; consumer products and live experiences&#59; games&#59; monetization through pricing and tiering structures, including paid sharing&#59; ad-supported tier and its prospects&#59; ads business&#59; product features&#59; acquisitions&#59; impact of foreign exchange rates&#59; foreign currency exchange hedging program&#59; seasonality&#59; cash balance and spend&#59; stock repurchases&#59; debt repayment&#59; paid net additions, membership growth and retention&#59; engagement&#59; consolidated revenue, revenue growth&#59; ARM, operating income, operating margin, net income, content amortization, and earnings per share&#59; and free cash flow.
